Refutation of an Objection on Divine Speech
Maturidi refutes an objection about speech using rational argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi refutes the objection that God cannot be described as speaking if He is silent or incapable, and the rationale behind His attributes.

Core Idea
God's attributes are not dependent on created states; He is eternally capable and speaking.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi answers a common challenge: how can God be described as 'Speaker' when speech implies change or ability? He shows that the objection is based on a misunderstanding of divine capability. By examining the example of a child, he clarifies that God is not like created beings.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and initial response
Read the Arabic and translation for the first part, where the opponent claims that someone who is silent cannot be described as speaking.
2
Analyze the counterexample of the child
Notice how Maturidi shows that the child is not a valid analogy for God, because God is not incapacitated like a child.
3
Understand the final answer
The capable agent remains capable even when acting; thus God's speech does not imply change.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مَنْ يجوز منه الكلام من خرس أو سكوت، وقد أخطأ في السؤال، إنما هو من عجز أو سكوت وعارض بالفعل، وهو كذلك عند الخصم. مع ما ذكر فيه الفعل أو الترك، وما الترك إلا الفعل، لكن الحيرة تعمل به ما ذكر. ثم عارض بالصبي أنه ليس بأخرس، وقد بينا أنه يعجز عن ذلك مع ما كان من عِظَم عجزه أن لا يجد لنفسه مثلا يعرف به الرب إلا الصبيان والمجانين. ولا قوة إلا بالله. وأجاب لما عورض بما لا يخلو القادر - مما له القدرة من فعل وكلام به ـ في حال حدوث القدرة من فعل. وذلك جهل المعتزلة جَعَله دليلاً، فبورك له في توحيده الذي ذلك دليله. {قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : } والأصل في ذلك أن الوصف بالكلام والعلم والفعل والحمد عليه إنما هو وصف بالبراءة من الآفات والتعالى عن العيوب، وهو كذلك في الأزل. مع ما لو كان بغيره خالقا رحمانًا متكلما يجوز أن يصير لا كذلك والقول بـ «يا مَنْ ليس برحمن ولا رحيم ولا خالق قول ذمّ وإلحاق بغيره من الخلائق، فثبت أنه بذاته رحمن رحيم خالق. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
Who can speak from dumbness or silence? He erred in the question. It is only from incapacity or silence, and he countered with action, and it is so with the opponent. Along with what was mentioned therein of action or abandonment, and abandonment is only action, but confusion operates with what was mentioned. Then he countered with the child that he is not dumb, and we have shown that he is incapable of that, along with the greatness of his incapacity that he does not find for himself an example by which he knows the Lord except children and the insane. And there is no power except with Allah. And he answered: When it was countered with what the capable one — who has power over action and speech — does not lack in the state of the occurrence of power from action. And that is the ignorance of the Mu`tazila which he made a proof, so blessed is he in his tawhid which has that as its proof. {Abu Mansur said, may Allah have mercy on him:} The foundation in that is that description with speech, knowledge, action, and praise is only a description of being free from defects and exalted above faults, and it is so in pre-eternity. Along with that, if He were by other than Himself Creator, Merciful, Speaker, it would be possible that He becomes not so, and saying 'O He who is not Merciful nor Compassionate nor Creator' is a word of blame and attribution to other than Him of creatures. So it is established that He is by His Essence Merciful, Compassionate, Creator. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer followed by a doctrinal principle. The opponent objects: If someone is incapable of speech, how can he be described as speaking? Maturidi responds that the objection misses the point: the one who is silent or incapable is not a speaker, but the one who has power over speech is. He then addresses a counterexample about a child, showing that children and madmen are not models for understanding God. The response to the objection is that the capable agent does not cease to be capable in the moment of action. Maturidi then states the foundational principle: describing God with speech, knowledge, action, and praise is actually describing that He is free from defects and exalted above faults. This applies from pre-eternity. If God were Merciful or Creator by something other than His Essence, He could cease to be so, which is impermissible. Thus, God is by His Essence Merciful, Compassionate, Creator.

قدرة
خرس
سكوت

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that if God is described as speaking, He must undergo change like humans.
Correction: Maturidi shows that divine capability is eternal and does not require change; speech is an attribute of perfection.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi say about the child as an example for understanding God?
A) The child is a perfect analogy
B) The child is incapable and thus not a valid example
C) The child is dumb
D) The child has power over speech

Key Takeaway
God's speech is an eternal attribute of His essence, not dependent on created events.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt that God is silent in response to your prayers, and in that silence doubted His power to hear you? How does this lesson's distinction between silence and incapacity change how you view those moments? Commit to trusting His eternal capability even when you do not perceive a response.
?
When you describe God's attributes, do you unconsciously limit them by comparing them to your own? This lesson refutes using human analogies like the child. In what area of your life do you most struggle to conceive of God's perfection without reducing it to human terms? Resolve to actively correct that misconception today.
?
The opponent in this passage used a flawed rational argument about speech. How often do you rely on your own reasoning to understand God, rather than submitting to what revelation and sound theology teach? Will you examine your assumptions and repent of any intellectual pride?

Divine Attributes as Descriptions of Perfection
Maturidi establishes the intrinsic nature of divine attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that describing God with attributes like mercy and creation is actually proclaiming His freedom from defects and that these attributes are intrinsic to His essence.

Core Idea
Divine attributes are not accidental additions; they are descriptions of God's inherent perfection.

Imam Maturidi now states a foundational principle: when we say God is knowing, merciful, creator, we are not describing Him with qualities that come and go, but rather we are declaring that He is free from all defects and exalted above any imperfection. This applies from pre-eternity, and if these attributes were from another, God could cease to be so.

Guided Path
1
Read the principle
Read the passage from 'The foundation in that...' to the end. Notice the key claim that description with attributes is really description with being free from defects.
2
Consider the consequence
If attributes were from another, God could change. Maturidi shows this is impossible, so attributes are by His essence.
3
Reflect on the concluding statement
The passage ends with 'So it is established...' — this is the conclusion that God is by His essence Merciful, Compassionate, Creator.

Source Text

Attributes Are Real and Distinct: Maturidi's Refutation
Maturidi criticizes the opponent's claim that attributes are speech or writing and not distinct.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's refutation of the claim that divine attributes are merely speech or writing and not real distinct entities.

Core Idea
Divine attributes are real and distinct from the essence, not mere speech.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi responds to a theological opponent who reduces divine attributes to speech or writing, denying their reality. Maturidi exposes the logical inconsistency in the opponent's view and affirms that the attributes of the Essence (ṣifāt al-dhāt) are distinct (aghyār) and eternal, not originated.

Guided Path
1
Read the opponent's claim
Start by reading the opponent's statement in the first part of the Arabic passage. Notice how he defines attributes as speech or writing and says they are not distinct 'others'.
The opponent tries to avoid affirming attributes as real.
2
Identify Maturidi's first critique
After the opponent's statement, Maturidi comments that the opponent's position contradicts the 'people of affirmation' (Ahl al-Ithbāt). He points out the confusion: if attributes are neither God nor other, what are they?
3
Observe Maturidi's own stance
Maturidi then presents the correct view: attributes of the Essence (ṣifāt al-dhāt) are other (aghyār) to Him, and He is eternally described by them. This refutes the opponent's reductionism.
Note the term aghyār – it affirms real distinction.
4
Analyze the mercy example
Finally, Maturidi addresses an objection about the attribute of mercy. The opponent claims that the attribute is the statement 'I am Merciful' rather than an actual quality. Maturidi uses this to show the absurdity of the opponent's position.
This seals the refutation by concrete example.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم قال : نريد بصفات أن لا يثبت ثَمَّةَ غير، ولم نرد أنها ذاته، بل كل صفة لقديم أو حديث فهي غيره؛ وهي قول أو كتاب. وصفات الله هي قولنا الذي يصفه، أو قوله وكتابه، وهما محدثان. { قال أبو منصو رضي الله عنه : } ذكرت جملة قوله الذي ختم [به] مسألته لتعلموا مبلغ علمه بالله ثم بالصفات مرةً قال : لا يثبت ثمة غير ولا يريد أنها هو، فإذا لم يُرد بالصفات هو ولا غيره، أما يعلم أنه قول أهل الإثبات. ثم قال : هي قولنا. فقولنا : هي ليست غيره حتى نقول: ليس ثمة غير. ثم ذكر أن صفات الله ما ذكر، وقال: هي صفات الذات، وهو لم يزل بها موصوفا وهي أغيار له، جل ربنا عما يصفه هي صفات الذات. فإذا ما ذكر هي المبطلون. ثم قال : فإن قيل : لِمَ لا جعلتم الرحمة صفة في الحقيقة، دون أن نقول: «رحيم»؟ فزعم أن رحيم صفة، دون الرحمة؛ إذ كل من فعل صفة الشيء فقد وصفه، كمن يشتم آخر أو يسوده أنه شتمه وسوّدَه، فكذلك خلق الرحمة، ولا يجوز أن يوصف بها إذ خلقها حتى يقول إني رحيم. فبذلك علمنا أن الصفة قوله : إنه رحيم.
Then he said: We mean by attributes that no other is established there, and we do not mean that they are His essence, but every attribute of an eternal or originated thing is other than it; and it is speech or writing. And the attributes of God are our speech by which we describe Him, or His speech and His book, and both are originated. {Abu Mansur said, may Allah be pleased with him:} I mentioned the summary of his statement with which he concluded his question to let you know the extent of his knowledge of God and then of the attributes. He once said: No other is established there, and he does not mean that they are He. So when he does not mean by the attributes He nor other, does he not know that this is the statement of the people of affirmation? Then he said: They are our speech. So our speech: they are not other than Him until we say: there is no other. Then he mentioned that the attributes of God are what he mentioned, and he said: They are attributes of the Essence, and He does not cease to be described by them, and they are others (aghyar) to Him, exalted is our Lord above what they describe — they are attributes of the Essence. So what he mentioned are the invalidators. Then he said: If it is said: Why did you not make mercy a real attribute, without us saying 'Merciful'? He claimed that 'Merciful' is an attribute, not mercy; because everyone who does the attribute of a thing has described it, like one who insults another or makes him a master — that he insulted him and made him a master. So likewise, the creation of mercy, and it is not permissible to be described by it since He created it, unless He says 'I am Merciful'. By that we know that the attribute is His saying: He is Merciful.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a detailed critique of an opponent's view on divine attributes. The opponent states that by 'attributes' he means that there is no distinct other entity, and attributes are merely speech or writing, and thus originated. Maturidi then comments, showing the confusion: if the opponent says attributes are neither God nor other, that contradicts the position of the people of affirmation (Ahl al-Ithbat). The opponent later claims that attributes like 'Merciful' are the statement itself, not a real quality. Maturidi exposes the absurdity: attributing mercy to God is His own declaration, not a real attribute He possesses. This leads to a denial of real divine attributes.

Key Terms
صفات الذات
أغيار
إثبات
قول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Divine attributes are merely mental concepts or speech, not real distinct entities.
Correction: Maturidi argues that attributes of the Essence are real, distinct (aghyār), and eternal, not mere speech or writing.

Checkpoint
What does the opponent claim about the attribute 'Mercy'?
A) It is a real quality inherent in God
B) It is a created thing
C) It is only God's saying 'I am Merciful'
D) It is the same as God's essence

Key Takeaway
Imam Maturidi refutes the claim that divine attributes are mere speech, affirming they are real, distinct, and eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite 'Ar-Rahman, Ar-Rahim' in your daily prayers, do you truly believe that mercy is a real, eternal attribute in Allah's essence, or do you think of it as just a comforting description? What would change in your reverence if you fully internalized that Allah has always been Merciful without beginning?
?
Maturidi exposes the absurdity of the opponent's view. Is there any belief you hold about Allah's attributes that, if pressed logically, would collapse like the opponent's? Are you willing to let Maturidi's correction dismantle comfortable but inconsistent ideas you may have harbored?
?
The opponent argued that the attribute is the statement 'I am Merciful', not mercy itself. Have you ever treated Allah's names as mere labels, using them without pondering their reality? How would your worship shift if you meditated on each name as a distinct, eternal truth about your Lord?

Refutation of the Analogy of Redness in Cloth for Divine Attributes
Maturidi refutes the opponent's analogy of red color in cloth to deny real attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi rejects the comparison of God's attributes to accidental qualities like redness in a garment, and how he argues that attributes are real and inherent in essences.

Core Idea
God's attributes are essential, not accidental qualities added by description.

Maturidi confronts an opponent who likens divine attributes to created accidents, such as redness in a cloth. The opponent argues that since redness is not truly an attribute of the cloth but merely a description, likewise God's attributes are not real. In this passage, Maturidi refutes this by showing that attributes in creation are intrinsic and do not depend on a describer. This sets the stage for affirming that God's attributes are real and eternal.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and English to grasp Maturidi's tone and argument.
The passage is dense and polemical.
2
Identify the opponent's analogy
The opponent says that when God creates redness in a garment, it does not become an attribute of God. Find this in the text.
3
Understand Maturidi's counter-argument
Maturidi argues that attributes in created things are not merely descriptions but are inherent. Note his examples of motion and stillness.
4
Reflect on the consequence for divine attributes
The refutation implies that God's attributes, unlike created accidents, are essential and not subject to change.

{ قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : } ما أعرف هذا التائه بالصفات حتى يشرع في تفسير صفات الله جلّ الله عن مثل هذا الخيال وتعالى. ولو كانت الصفة في الحقيقة وصف الواصف ليبطل قول الخلق بأن الخلق أعيان وصفات، ويبطل قوله في الاجتماع والتفرق والحركة والسكون التي لا تخلو الأعيان عنها في إثبات حدثها، إذ هي تخلو عن وصف واصف لها. فثبت أنها صفات تلزم الأعيان، لا ما ذكر. ولا قوة إلا بالله. ثم تتمّ هذا النوع من حماقته لتحمدوا الله، معاشر إخواني، على ما أكرمكم الله بمعرفته، ولتعلموا عظيم مقت الله على من زعم أنه قد استوعب جميع ما عند الله من المصالح له في الدين؛ حتى لو أراد الله أن يزيد له شيئًا لا يملكه مما به صلاحه، لا يقدر عليه، بل به يفسد؛ و لتتبينوا أنه جعل خذلانه صلاحًا في الدين وإضلاله نعمة من نعم الرب جل ثناؤه. قال: لم نقل : إن الله إذا خلق الحمرة في الثوب أنه جعل له صفة. ولو كانت الحمرة صفة له جاز أن يقال إذ خلقها الله : وصف الثوب بها، ومثله في الحركة والسكون. وكذا من يكتب
{Abu Mansur said, may Allah have mercy on him:} I do not know this confused one about attributes until he begins to interpret the attributes of God — exalted is God above such imagination. And if the attribute in reality were the description of the describer, it would invalidate the statement of creation that creatures are essences and attributes, and it would invalidate his statement about conjunction, separation, motion, and stillness, which essences do not lack in establishing their origination, since they are devoid of the description of a describer for them. So it is established that they are attributes that adhere to essences, not what he mentioned. And there is no power except with Allah. Then complete this type of his foolishness so that you may praise Allah, O my brothers, for what Allah has honored you with knowledge, and so that you may realize the great anger of Allah against one who claims that he has comprehended all the benefits from Allah for him in religion; such that if Allah wanted to add something to him which he does not possess of what constitutes his well-being, he cannot, but rather it corrupts him; and so that you may realize that he made his abandonment a benefit in religion and his misguidance a blessing from the blessings of the Lord, exalted is His praise. He said: We did not say: When Allah creates redness in a garment, that He made an attribute for it. And if the redness were an attribute of it, it would be permissible to say, when Allah created it, that He described the garment with it, and likewise in motion and stillness. And likewise one who writes

Commentary
This passage is a vehement refutation of an opponent's analogy between divine attributes and accidental qualities like redness in a cloth. Maturidi begins by expressing shock at the opponent's confusion. He argues that if an attribute were merely the description of a describer, then created things would not have intrinsic attributes. But in fact, attributes like conjunction, separation, motion, and stillness are inherent in created essences and do not require an external describer. Therefore, attributes are real and adhere to the object. He then criticizes the opponent's arrogance in claiming to have full knowledge of divine purposes. The opponent's example: if God creates redness in a garment, that does not make the redness an attribute of God. The opponent uses this to deny that God's attributes are real. Maturidi implies that this reasoning is flawed because it confuses accidental qualities in creation with essential attributes of the Creator.

Correction: Maturidi shows that attributes in created things are intrinsic and do not depend on a describer; likewise, God's attributes are essential and real, not accidental.

Attributes Are Real, Not Mere Descriptions
Maturidi refutes a view that reduces real attributes to mere verbal descriptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that divine attributes are real attributes inherent in the essence, not merely verbal descriptions.

Core Idea
If attributes were just words, created things would lose their real qualities.

This passage tackles a critical debate: Are God's attributes real distinct meanings or just labels? An opponent claims they are mere descriptions. Maturidi refutes this by showing that if attributes were only descriptions, then creatures would not have real qualities like motion. He also warns that such a view leads to arrogance and misguidance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the full translation to grasp the flow of argument.
Notice the opponent's analogy with 'Merciful' and 'mercy'.
2
Identify the opponent's claim and Maturidi's counter
The opponent says the attribute is the description (e.g., 'Merciful') not the reality (mercy). Maturidi counters with examples from creation: motion and stillness are real attributes even when not described.
Ask yourself: why does Maturidi use motion as an example?
3
Reflect on the warning
Maturidi warns that this mistaken view leads to claiming one has fully encompassed divine benefit, implying God cannot add more. Consider why he calls this 'foolishness' and a cause of divine wrath.
This connects doctrine to the state of the believer's heart.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو منصور رضي الله عنه : ذكرت جملة قوله الذي ختم مسألته لتعلموا مبلغ علمه بالله ثم بالصفات مرةً قال : لا يثبت ثمة غير ولا يريد أنها هو ، فإذا لم يُرد بالصفات هو ولا غيره، أما يعلم أنه قول أهل الإثبات . ثم قال : هي قولنا. فقولنا : هي ليست غيره حتى نقول: ليس ثمة غير . ثم ذكر أن صفات الله ما ذكر، وقال: هي صفات الذات، وهو لم يزل بها موصوفا وهي أغيار له، جل ربنا عما يصفه هي صفات الذات. فإذا ما ذكر هي المبطلون. ثم قال : فإن قيل : لِمَ لا جعلتم الرحمة صفة في الحقيقة، دون أن نقول: «رحيم»؟ فزعم أن رحيم صفة، دون الرحمة؛ إذ كل من فعل صفة الشيء فقد وصفه، كمن يشتم آخر أو يسوده أنه شتمه وسوّدَه ، فكذلك خلق الرحمة، ولا يجوز أن يوصف بها إذ خلقها حتى يقول إني رحيم. فبذلك علمنا أن الصفة قوله : إنه رحيم.

{ قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : } ما أعرف هذا التائه بالصفات حتى يشرع في تفسير صفات الله جلّ الله عن مثل هذا الخيال وتعالى. ولو كانت الصفة في الحقيقة وصف الواصف ليبطل قول الخلق بأن الخلق أعيان وصفات، ويبطل قوله في الاجتماع والتفرق والحركة والسكون التي لا تخلو الأعيان عنها في إثبات حدثها ، إذ هي تخلو عن وصف واصف لها . فثبت أنها صفات تلزم الأعيان، لا ما ذكر . ولا قوة الا بالله . ثم تتمّ هذا النوع من حماقته لتحمدوا الله ، معاشر إخواني، على ما أكرمكم الله بمعرفته، ولتعلموا عظيم مقت الله على من زعم أنه قد استوعب جميع ما عند الله من المصالح له في الدين ؛ حتى لو أراد الله أن يزيد له شيئًا لا يملكه مما به صلاحه ، لا يقدر عليه، بل به يفسد ؛ و لتتبينوا أنه جعل خذلانه صلاحًا في الدين وإضلاله نعمة من نعم الرب جل ثناؤه.
Abu Mansur (may Allah be pleased with him) said: I mentioned the sum of his statement with which he concluded his question, so that you may know the extent of his knowledge of Allah, then of the attributes. He said once: There is no 'other' established there, and he does not intend that they are 'He'. So when he does not intend by the attributes 'He' nor 'other', does he not know that this is the statement of the people of affirmation? Then he said: They are our statement. So our statement is: They are not other than Him, so that we may say: There is no 'other' there. Then he mentioned that the attributes of Allah are what he mentioned, and said: They are attributes of the Essence (ṣifāt al-dhāt), and He has never ceased to be described by them, and they are distinct from Him (aghyār lahu). Exalted is our Lord above what they describe! They are attributes of the Essence. Then when he mentioned what the invalidators mention. Then he said: If it is said: Why did you not make mercy (al-raḥma) a real attribute (ṣifa fī al-ḥaqīqa), instead of saying 'Merciful'? So he claimed that 'Merciful' is the attribute, not mercy, because whoever acts upon the attribute of a thing has described it, like one who insults another or makes him a master, that he insulted him and made him a master. Likewise, [God] created mercy, and it is not permissible for Him to be described by it since He created it, until He says 'I am Merciful'. Thus we know that the attribute is His statement: He is Merciful.

Abu Mansur (may Allah have mercy on him) said: I do not recognize this confused one (al-tā'ih) concerning the attributes, so that he ventures into interpreting the attributes of Allah—exalted is Allah above such imagination! And if the attribute in reality were the description of the describer, then the statement of the creation that the creation are entities (a'yān) and attributes would be invalid, and his statement about conjunction and separation, motion and stillness—which entities never lack—would be invalid in establishing their temporality, since they lack a describer's description of them. So it is established that they are attributes that adhere to entities, not what he mentioned. And there is no power except with Allah. Then complete this type of his foolishness, so that you may praise Allah, O my brothers, for what Allah has honored you with knowing, and so that you may know the greatness of Allah's wrath upon one who claims that he has encompassed all that Allah has of benefits for him in religion, such that even if Allah wished to add something for him which he does not possess of what is for his well-being, he is unable to do so; rather, it would corrupt him. And so that you may realize that he made his abandonment a benefit in religion and his misguidance a blessing from the blessings of the Lord, majestic is His praise.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a specific view regarding the nature of divine attributes. It begins by quoting an opponent who claims that attributes are not real entities distinct from God, but merely descriptions (like saying 'Merciful'). The opponent argues that the attribute is the statement 'Merciful', not the reality of mercy. The author (Maturidi) then responds by identifying this opponent as confused (tā'ih). He argues that if attributes were merely descriptions, then created entities would not have real attributes like conjunction or motion, since they can exist without being described. This proves attributes are real properties of entities. He then warns that this misguided view leads to a dangerous claim: that one has fully comprehended all divine benefits, implying God cannot add more. Such a person mistakes his own abandonment for divine favor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Attributes are merely descriptions (sayings) and have no real existence in God's essence.
Correction: Attributes are real meanings (ṣifāt) inhering in the essence, distinct from the essence and from each other, as proven by the reality of attributes in created entities like motion.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the consequence of saying attributes are merely descriptions?
A) It leads to denying God's existence.
B) It would invalidate the reality of qualities like motion in created entities.
C) It means mercy is not a real attribute of God.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi establishes that divine attributes are real, not just words, by pointing out that created attributes (like motion) are real and not dependent on being described.

Now apply that to Allah: do you live as if His attributes are real, present, and active even when you do not feel or articulate them? What one change would this truth demand of you today?

Refutation of Analogies Between Divine and Created Attributes
Maturidi refutes analogies comparing divine attributes to created properties like redness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi rejects the analogy that divine attributes are merely descriptive, like redness in a garment, and how the Mu'tazili position leads to logical contradictions.

Core Idea
Comparing God's attributes to created qualities destroys their reality.

In this passage, Imam al-Maturidi tackles a key Mu'tazili argument: that divine attributes such as mercy are not real attributes of God but merely descriptions of His actions, just as redness created in a garment is not an attribute of the garment itself. The opponent uses examples from everyday language to deny the reality of attributes. Maturidi exposes the flaw in this analogy and shows how it leads to absurd consequences, while the jurist (al-faqīh) delivers a scathing critique of those who follow such reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the opponent's claim
The opponent argues that when God creates redness in a garment, He does not make an attribute for the garment. Instead, the garment is merely described as red. Similarly, mercy is an attribute of the act, not of God. Read the passage to see exactly how the opponent frames this analogy.
Notice the examples: redness, motion, stillness, writing a letter.
2
Identify Maturidi's implicit response
Maturidi does not directly rebut the claim here; instead he quotes the opponent's admission that such statements are metaphorical. This suggests the opponent is conflating metaphor with reality. Reflect on why this is a weak argument.
The key terms are 'majāz' (metaphor) and 'ḥaqīqa' (reality).
3
Trace the objection and counter-response
The opponent objects: if redness is an attribute, then attributes could themselves have attributes. Maturidi replies that description depends on the describer's act and ceases when he stops. This shows the opponent's view makes attributes dependent on human speech, not real.
Think about what this implies for God's attributes.
4
Understand the jurist's condemnation
The jurist severely criticizes the Mu'tazila for following such flawed reasoning. He warns that this line of thought leads to misguidance on the Day of Judgment. This is a strong rhetorical conclusion.
Consider why the jurist uses such harsh language.
5
Connect to the broader lesson on divine attributes
This passage illustrates a central issue in kalām: are God's attributes real and eternal, or merely descriptions? The Mu'tazili position reduces them to metaphors, which Maturidi rejects as inconsistent with tawḥīd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال: لم نقل: إن الله إذا خلق الحمرة في الثوب أنه جعل له صفة. ولو كانت الحمرة صفة له جاز أن يقال إذ خلقها الله : وصف الثوب بها، ومثله في الحركة والسكون. وكذا من يكتب إلى آخر يصف طوله ، يجوز أن يُقال : وصفه لنا في كتابه زعم أن هذا واضح. ثم قال: وإنّا لا ننكر جواز إطلاق القول بأن الحمرة صفة الأحمر، والرحمة صفة الفعل، لكن على المجاز والحقيقة ما ذكرت . ثم عورض بأنه يجوز إذا أن يكون للصفة صفة . قال : نعم، بمعنى أنها توصف، لكن ذلك إنما يوجد ما دام الواصف به قائلاً، فإذا أمسك لا . قال الفقيه رحمه الله : تأملوا عظيم منزلة المعتزلة بالائتمام بهذا الذي هذا مبلغ علمه بالصفة والموصوف والمجاز والحقيقة مما لو قرف به أجهل أهل توحيد الله لاستعظموه. ثم يقدم قومه يوم القيامة فيوردهم المورد الذي هذا وصف سبيله. نسأل الله العصمة.
He said: We do not say that when God creates redness (al-ḥumra) in a garment, He has made an attribute for it. And if redness were an attribute of it, it would be permissible to say, when God created it, that He described the garment with it; and similarly for motion and stillness. Likewise, one who writes to another describing his height, it is permissible to say: he described him in his book. He claimed that this is clear. Then he said: And we do not deny the permissibility of saying that redness is an attribute of the red thing, and mercy is an attribute of the act, but as for metaphor (al-majāz) and reality (al-ḥaqīqa), it is as I mentioned. Then it was objected: Then it is permissible for an attribute to have an attribute. He said: Yes, in the sense that it is described, but that only exists as long as the describer is speaking; when he stops, [it does not]. The jurist (al-faqīh) (may Allah have mercy on him) said: Reflect on the great station of the Mu'tazila in following this one, whose knowledge of the attribute, the described, metaphor and reality is such that if the most ignorant of the people of tawḥīd were accused of it, he would find it enormous. Then he will lead his people on the Day of Resurrection and lead them to the watering place which is described thus. We ask Allah for protection.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage rebuts a second objection that uses analogies from created things to deny real divine attributes. The opponent argues that redness created in a garment is not an attribute of the garment; rather, the garment is described as red by virtue of that redness. Similarly, they argue that God's mercy should be seen as an attribute of the act, not of God Himself. The author's response is implicit: he quotes the opponent's admission that such statements are metaphorical, not real. When further pressed that attributes themselves could have attributes, the opponent concedes that description depends on the speaker's act, implying attributes are not real. The jurist then severely criticizes the Mu'tazila for following such flawed reasoning, warning that this leads to misguidance.

صفة الفعل
مجاز
حقيقة
واصف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That divine attributes like mercy are merely descriptions of God's actions, not real attributes of His essence.
Correction: The passage shows that reducing attributes to metaphors or descriptions leads to absurdities; attributes are real and rooted in God's essence, not dependent on human speech.

Checkpoint
What does the opponent concede about calling redness an attribute?
A) It is absolutely true in reality.
B) It is permissible only as metaphor.
C) It is false because attributes cannot be described.
D) It is valid only if God wills.

Key Takeaway
Reducing God's attributes to metaphors or descriptions undermines their reality and leads to theological incoherence.

?

?
The Mu'tazili reduced God's attributes to human descriptions. Is there any area of your theology where you let your own reasoning limit God's reality? What step will you take today to submit to the truth of His attributes as they are in themselves?

Two Proofs That God Speaks
Maturidi provides transmitted and rational proofs that God has the attribute of speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses both transmitted (Quranic) and rational arguments to establish that God has the attribute of speech.

Core Idea
God speaks; proof comes from scripture and from reason.

Maturidi presents a concise twofold argument that God has the attribute of speech (kalām). He first cites Quranic verses and consensus, then gives a rational argument based on the impossibility of imperfection in God. This lesson unpacks both proofs and shows how they complement each other.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic source and its translation. Notice that Maturidi begins with a principle and then gives two types of proof.
The passage is dense; read slowly.
2
Identify the transmitted proof
Find the Quranic evidence and the mention of consensus. Understand how these establish God's speech.
The verses are from Surat al-Nisa' and al-Baqara.
3
Understand the rational proof
The rational argument focuses on imperfection. If a knowing, powerful being does not speak, it must be due to an infirmity, which is impossible for Allah.
Also note the comparison to deafness, blindness, and muteness.
4
Reflect on the unity of the proofs
Both proofs independently establish the same attribute. Consider why both are needed.
This reflects the Maturidi methodology of combining revelation and reason.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : الأصل أن الله عز وجل قد ثبت وصفه بالكلام بحجة السمع والعقل . فالسمع قوله : وكلّم الله موسى تكليما (النساء، 164) ذكره بالمصدر. مع غير تمانع بين الخلق بكلام الله ، وقد وجد الاتفاق على أنه متكلم وأن له كلاما في الحقيقة وإن اختلفت في مائيته. ولا أنكر على الذين قالوا لولا يكلّمنا الله (البقرة، 118) إلا : بوصف التكبر والجهل بمنزلة أنفسهم ؛ وكذلك قوله : وقد كان فريق منهم يسمعون كلام الله (البقرة، 75). وأما العقل، إن كل عالم قادر لا يتكلم فعن آفة يكون : من عجز أو منع، والله عنه متعال، ثبت أنه متكلم . على أن الذي لا يتكلم في الشاهد إنما لا يتكلم بالمعنى الذي لا يسمع ولا يبصر من الآفة، والله منزه عن المعنى الذي يقتضي الصَّمَم والعَمَى ؛ وكذلك البكم، وهو أولى، إذ هو أجل ما يُحمد به في الشاهد وبه ينفصل البشر من سائر الحيوان. مع ما كان كل محتمل
Abu Mansur (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The principle is that Allah, mighty and majestic, is established to be described with speech (kalām) by proof from transmitted report (sam') and reason ('aql). As for the transmitted report, it is His statement: 'And Allah spoke to Moses directly' (Qur'an 4:164), mentioning it with the verbal noun. There is no disagreement among people concerning the speech of Allah, and consensus has been found that He is speaking (mutakallim) and that He has speech in reality, even if they differ about its essence. He did not deny against those who said 'Why does not Allah speak to us?' (Qur'an 2:118) except [that they did so] with the description of arrogance and ignorance about their own status; and likewise His statement: 'And a group of them used to listen to the speech of Allah' (Qur'an 2:75). As for reason, every knowing and powerful being who does not speak does so due to an infirmity: either incapacity or prevention, and Allah is exalted above that; so it is established that He is speaking. Moreover, one who does not speak in the physical world only does not speak due to the meaning that makes him unable to hear or see from infirmity, and Allah is transcendent above the meaning that necessitates deafness and blindness; and similarly for muteness (al-bakam)—and this [speech] is more appropriate, for it is the greatest thing for which humans are praised in the physical world, and by it humans are distinguished from other animals. With what was every potential...
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage presents a twofold proof that God has the attribute of speech (kalām). The transmitted proof cites Quranic verses showing God spoke to Moses and that people listened to His speech, and notes consensus that God is speaking. The rational proof argues that a knowing, powerful being who does not speak does so only due to an imperfection (incapacity or prevention). Since God is free from such imperfections, He must speak. Furthermore, in the physical world, the inability to speak is related to the same deficiency that causes deafness and blindness, from which God is far removed. Speech is also the highest human virtue and what distinguishes humans from animals, so it is even more fitting for God.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think rational proof alone cannot establish that God speaks, but the passage shows both transmitted and rational proofs are used together.
Correction: The passage actually provides both proofs, and each independently supports the attribute of speech. The rational proof is valid on its own, but Maturidi presents both to strengthen the case.

God's Speech: Evidence from Revelation and Reason
Maturidi's proof for God's speech from scripture and reason.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Maturidi establishes God's attribute of speech using both scriptural evidence and rational argument.

Core Idea
God's speech is proven by both revelation and reason, addressing a fundamental divine attribute.

In this passage, Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi presents the foundational proof for God's attribute of speech (kalām). He argues that both the Qur'an and rational necessity confirm that Allah speaks. The passage combines a scriptural citation and a logical inference from negation of defects. Let's examine his argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic text and its literal translation carefully. Notice the clear division between the two types of evidence: samʿ (revelation) and ʿaql (reason).
2
Identify the scriptural evidence
Find the verses cited by Maturidi. What do they indicate about God's speech? Note that he emphasizes the consensus of the community and the rebuke of those who questioned.
3
Analyze the rational argument
Maturidi argues that a knowing, powerful being that does not speak must have a defect. Since God is free from defects, He must speak. Consider how this logical inference works.
4
Reflect on the implications
Think about why this attribute is important in Islamic theology. How does this proof connect to other divine attributes?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو منصور رحمه الله: الأصل أن الله عز وجل قد ثبت وصفه بالكلام بحجة السمع والعقل. فالسمع قوله: {وكلّم الله موسى تكليما} [النساء 164] ذكره بالمصدر. مع غير تمانع بين الخلق بكلام الله، وقد وجد الاتفاق على أنه متكلم وأن له كلاما في الحقيقة وإن اختلفت في مائيته. ولا أنكر على الذين قالوا {لولا يكلّمنا الله} [البقرة 118] إلا بوصف التكبر والجهل بمنزلة أنفسهم؛ وكذلك قوله: {وقد كان فريق منهم يسمعون كلام الله} [البقرة 75]. وأما العقل، إن كل عالم قادر لا يتكلم فعن آفة يكون: من عجز أو منع، والله عنه متعال، ثبت أنه متكلم. على أن الذي لا يتكلم في الشاهد إنما لا يتكلم بالمعنى الذي لا يسمع ولا يبصر من الآفة، والله منزه عن المعنى الذي يقتضي الصّمم والعَمى؛ وكذلك البكم، وهو أولى، إذ هو أجل ما يُحمد به في الشاهد وبه ينفصل البشر من سائر الحيوان. مع ما كان كل محتمل الكلام فعن عجز لا يتكلم أو عن سكوت.
Abu Mansur, may Allah have mercy on him, said: The principle is that Allah, Mighty and Majestic, has His attribute of speech established by the evidence of revelation (samʿ) and reason (ʿaql). As for revelation, His saying: {And Allah spoke to Moses directly} [al-Nisa: 164] – He mentioned it with the verbal noun (maṣdar). Along with there being no mutual opposition among creation concerning the speech of Allah, and agreement has been found that He is a speaker and that He has speech in reality, even if they differed concerning its quiddity. And He did not deny those who said {Why does Allah not speak to us} [al-Baqara: 118] except by describing them as arrogant and ignorant of their own status; likewise His saying: {And a party of them used to hear the speech of Allah} [al-Baqara: 75]. As for reason, every knowing, powerful being that does not speak is [afflicted] by a defect: either incapacity or prevention, and Allah is exalted above that, so it is established that He is a speaker. Moreover, the one who does not speak in the witnessed world only does not speak due to a defect in the sense that he does not hear or see, and Allah is transcendent above the condition that entails deafness and blindness; likewise muteness, and it is more appropriate, for speech is the noblest thing for which one is praised in the witnessed world and by which humans are distinguished from other animals. And since every being capable of speech either does not speak due to incapacity or silence.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is a two-part proof for the divine attribute of speech (kalām), as presented by Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi. He begins by stating the principle: God's attribute of speech is established by both revelation (samʿ) and reason (ʿaql). First, the scriptural evidence: he cites the verse 'And Allah spoke to Moses directly' (al-Nisa 4:164), noting that the infinitive (تكليما) emphasizes the reality of the speech. He then appeals to consensus: the Muslim community agrees that God is a speaker and has real speech, though they differ on its nature. He interprets the verse 'Why does Allah not speak to us' (al-Baqara 2:118) as God's rebuke of the questioners' arrogance and ignorance, not a denial of His speech. Another verse (al-Baqara 2:75) confirms that some Israelites used to hear God's speech. Second, the rational argument: any being that is knowing and powerful yet does not speak must be afflicted by a defect—either inability or prevention—but God is exalted above such defects, so He must be a speaker. In the empirical world, non-speech results from a deficiency like deafness or blindness, and God is free from any such deficiency. Speech is also the noblest human quality that distinguishes humans from animals. Finally, whoever is capable of speech and does not speak does so only due to incapacity or silence, both inapplicable to God. Therefore, God is necessarily a speaker.

Key Terms
كلام
السمع
العقل
المتكلم
مائية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The rational proof for God's speech is independent of revelation.
Correction: Actually, the rational proof complements the scriptural evidence; both are needed to fully establish the attribute.

Checkpoint

B) Because of a defect such as incapacity or prevention.
C) Because the being chooses silence voluntarily.
D) Because speech would imply a body.

Key Takeaway
God's attribute of speech is rationally necessary and scripturally attested, forming a cornerstone of Islamic theology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

God's Speech is Unlike Created Speech: Negating Similarity
Negation of similarity, establishment of khilāfiyya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Maturidi uses Quranic verses to negate any similarity between God's speech and created speech, establishing the attribute of khilāfiyya (difference).

Core Idea
God’s speech is utterly different from created speech, just as His essence is.

Imam al-Maturidi begins by addressing a fundamental question: if God speaks, does His speech resemble the speech of creatures? He argues that any similarity would contradict the Quranic verse 'There is nothing like Him.' This lesson unpacks his argument that God's speech is categorically different from all created speech.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage slowly, then read the translation to get the gist of the argument.
2
Identify the key premise
Notice the logical structure: if God's speech were like another's, there would be similarity. Then the Quran negates that.
The verse from al-Shura is central.
3
Understand the ‘khilāfiyya’ concept
The conclusion is that God's speech is different (khilāf) from all created speech, just as His essence is different.
This is the anchor for eternity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم لا يخلو من أن يكون على تقدير كلام غيره فيكون فيه تشابه، ودل قوله: {وليس كمثله شيء} [الشورى 11] على نفي الشبه له في الصفة والذات؛ وأيّد ذا قوله: {خلقوا كخلقه} الآية، دل أن شبه الفعل يُوجب التشابه مع القول أن الخلق لو اجتمع لا يأتون بمثله، فانتفى الشبه، إذ فيه تماثل. فثبت له الخلافية لكلام الخلق جميعا على ما ثبت لذاته. مع ما لم يمتحن جميع كلام الخلق ليدرك منتهى معانيه. وقد ذكر كلام النمل والهدهد وتسبيح الجبال وغيرها مما لا يفهم شيء من ذلك بالحروف المعجمة ولا على المفهوم من كلام البشر. وإذ ثبت أن من الكلام ما لا يبلغ تقديره وسع الخلق ولا يبلغه فهم، فمن أحب تقدير كلام الرب بذلك فهو مغفّل وكذلك فعله تعالى خارج عن وصف فعل الخلق. وفي ثبوت الخلافية من جميع الوجوه نفي الحدثية، لما بها يقع الوفاق؛ وبطل معنى الأعراض من التفرق والاجتماع، والحد والغاية والزيادة والنقصان، إذ ذلك وصف كلام الخلق. والله الموفق. ثم لا يخلو من أن يكون غيره فيزول عنه ما ذكرنا من الآفة بغيره – وذلك علم الحاجة وأمارة الحدث - أو ليس غيره فيكون بنفسه متكلما قادرا عالما. وبالله التوفيق.
Then it cannot be free from being on the estimation of another's speech, for then there would be similarity, and His saying {And there is nothing like Him} [al-Shura 42:11] indicates the negation of similarity to Him in attribute and essence; and this is supported by His saying {They created like His creation} – the verse indicates that similarity in action necessitates similarity, along with the statement that if all creation gathered they could not produce its like, so similarity is negated, for then there would be likeness. So difference (al-khilāfiyya) is established for His speech over the speech of all creation, just as it is established for His essence. Moreover, not all the speech of creation has been examined to perceive the limit of its meanings. And He has mentioned the speech of the ant and the hoopoe and the glorification of the mountains and other things, none of which is understood through articulated letters (ḥurūf mujʿama) nor according to what is understood from human speech. And since it is established that there is speech whose estimation the capacity of creation does not reach nor does understanding reach it, then whoever desires to measure the speech of the Lord by that is a simpleton, and likewise His action, exalted is He, is outside the description of the actions of creation. And in the establishment of difference (al-khilāfiyya) from all aspects is the negation of temporality (al-ḥadathiyya), because by it agreement occurs; and the meaning of accidents (aʿrāḍ) of separation and union, limit and end, increase and decrease becomes invalid, for that is the description of the speech of creation. And Allah is the granter of success. Then it cannot be free from being other than Him, for then the defect we mentioned would be removed by another – and that is the sign of need and the mark of temporality; or it is not other than Him, so by Himself He is a speaker, powerful, knowing. And with Allah is success.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument proving that God's speech is eternal (qadīm) and utterly unlike created speech, thereby refuting the Mu'tazili claim that it is created (ḥadīth). The argument proceeds in several steps. First, if God's speech were like another's speech, there would be similarity (tashābuh), but the Quranic verse 'There is nothing like Him' (al-Shura 42:11) negates any similarity in attribute and essence. Another verse about 'they created like His creation' is cited to show that similarity in action would imply similarity, but creation cannot produce the like of God's speech, so similarity is negated. Therefore, God's speech is different (khilāfiyya) from all created speech, just as His essence is different. Second, even within creation, there are types of speech (e.g., the speech of ants and birds mentioned in the Quran) that are not understood through human letters or meanings, showing that speech can exist beyond human comprehension. Hence, it is foolish to try to measure God's speech by human standards. Third, from the complete difference (khilāfiyya) of God's speech from created speech, its non-temporality (nafy al-ḥadathiyya) is established, because temporality would involve agreement (wafāq) with changing states. Attributes of created speech such as separation, union, limit, increase, and decrease are thus negated for God's speech. Finally, a disjunctive argument: God's speech must either be other than Him (ghayruhu) or not. If it were other, that other would remove the defect of being unable to speak, implying need and temporality – impossible for God. Therefore, it is not other than Him; instead, by Himself (bi-nafsihi) He is a speaker, powerful, and knowing. This proves that God's speech is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence.

Key Terms
الخلافية
التشابه
التماثل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument uses similarity of action to prove similarity of essence; actually it refutes that.
Correction: The verse about 'similarity in action' is used to show that even if action were similar, it would necessitate similarity, but since creation cannot produce the like, similarity is negated. Thus, it does not prove similarity of essence; it reinforces difference.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the verse 'There is nothing like Him' indicate about God's speech?
A) It is similar to human speech in some ways.
B) It negates similarity in attribute and essence.
C) It supports the idea that God's speech is created.
D) It only applies to actions, not speech.

Key Takeaway
God's speech is absolutely different from all created speech, just as His essence is.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite or listen to the Quran, do you truly believe these words are unlike any human speech? How does that conviction change your attention and reverence?
?
If God’s speech is absolutely different from all created speech, then what does that mean for how you approach His Book? Are you treating it as ordinary words, or as something that demands a unique response?
?
The passage says no creature can produce the like of God’s speech. Have you ever tried to imitate or equal the Quran in your own thoughts or writings? What does that inability reveal about your own humility before Allah?

Eternity of God's Speech: Beyond Measure and Self-Subsisting
Proof of eternity via incomprehensibility, difference, and disjunctive argument

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Maturidi proves that God's speech is eternal (qadīm) by negating temporality and showing it is not other than God.

Core Idea
God's speech is eternal, beyond human measurement, and subsists by His own essence.

After establishing the absolute difference of God's speech, Imam al-Maturidi takes the argument further: this difference necessarily means His speech is not temporal. Moreover, the very nature of speech—some of which is beyond human comprehension—shows that measuring God's speech by human standards is foolish. Finally, a disjunctive argument proves that God's speech cannot be separate from His essence, but is an attribute subsisting in Him.

Guided Path
1
Read the second half of the passage
Begin from 'مع ما لم يمتحن' and read through to the end, noting the progression of ideas.
2
Understand the argument from incomprehensibility
The Quran mentions speech of creatures (ants, birds) that is not understood through human letters. This shows speech can exist beyond human measurement, so God's speech is even more so.
This refutes those who try to measure God's speech.
3
Analyze the disjunctive argument
The final part presents a two-option argument: either God's speech is other than Him or not. If it were other, that would imply need and temporality—impossible. Therefore, it is not other, meaning God is by Himself a speaker.
This proves the eternity and self-subsistence of the attribute.
4
Conclude with negation of temporality
From complete difference (khilāfiyya), temporality is negated, along with accidental properties like limit and increase.

Correction: The passage states that there is speech whose 'estimation the capacity of creation does not reach' – this indicates human limitation, not that the speech is inherently incomprehensible.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the establishment of difference from all aspects necessarily negate?
A) The existence of divine attributes.
B) The temporality of God's speech.
C) The possibility of human speech.
D) The diversity of creation.

Key Takeaway
God's speech is eternal because it is not other than Him and is free from all temporal attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you imagine God's speech, do you secretly measure it by human words, as the passage warns? In what specific way have you limited the Creator by your own understanding? Commit today to reminding yourself that His speech is beyond your capacity.
?
The disjunctive argument forces a choice: either you treat God's speech as something separate from Him, needing an external cause, or you accept that by His own essence He speaks, knows, and has power. Which side does your heart lean toward when you struggle with His decrees? How will you train your soul to see His attributes as inseparable from Him?
?
If God's speech is free from all accidents—no increase, decrease, limit—then no add to His words is possible. Yet we often feel we need more 'proof' or 'signs' to be certain. Does your faith rest on the eternal attribute or on fleeting feelings? What concrete step can you take today to anchor your certainty in the unchanging Word of God?

Calling Heard Speech 'God's Speech' Metaphorically
Ruling on metaphorically attributing created sounds to God's speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi ruling that audible expressions of God's speech can metaphorically be called 'the speech of Allah' on the basis of muwāfaqa (agreement).

Core Idea
Heard speech can be called God's speech metaphorically, not literally.

This lesson addresses a subtle but important theological-linguistic distinction: when a human recites the Quran, are those sounds properly called 'the speech of Allah'? Imam Maturidi gives a clear ruling based on the principle of muwāfaqa (agreement), drawing an analogy with letters and poems. Understanding this ruling helps avoid both crude anthropomorphism and the denial of God's eternal attribute of speech.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its literal translation. Notice the concise formulation of the ruling.
The passage is a single sentence with an analogy.
2
Understand 'muwāfaqa' and the analogy
The term 'muwāfaqa' (agreement/correspondence) indicates a metaphorical, not literal, attribution. The analogy with letters and poems clarifies that the creator of the content is called the speaker, even when the reciter produces the sounds.
This distinguishes between eternal divine speech and its temporal expression.
3
Appreciate theological balance
Reflect on how this ruling guards against two extremes: saying the recited Quran is eternal (like the Karramiyya) or denying that God has an attribute of speech.
The metaphor preserves both God's transcendence and the Quran's divine origin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز القول بما يُسمع من الخلق كلام الله على الموافقة كما يُقال في الرسائل والقصائد.
And it is permissible to say concerning what is heard from creation that it is the speech of Allah, on the basis of agreement (muwāfaqa), just as is said in letters and poems.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling on a linguistic issue: whether created sounds that convey God's speech (such as the recitation of the Quran by a human voice) can be called 'the speech of Allah'. The author permits this usage on the basis of 'muwāfaqa' (agreement or correspondence), meaning metaphorically or by way of attribution. He likens it to how one might say of a letter or poem that it is the speech of its author, even though the actual sounds are produced by the reciter. This clarifies that while God's speech is eternal and uncreated, the audible recitation is created but can be referred to as 'kalam Allah' in a metaphorical sense, not in the essential sense. The ruling guards against both the anthropomorphism of the Karramiyya (who would say the recitation itself is eternal) and the denial of God's attribute of speech by those who say only the recitation is God's speech literally.

Key Terms
كلام الله
الموافقة
الرسائل
القصائد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think this ruling means the recited Quran is created in every sense, denying that it is God's speech at all.
Correction: The passage distinguishes between eternal divine speech and its temporal expression; the recitation is created but metaphorically called God's speech because it corresponds to His eternal attribute.

Checkpoint
On what basis is it permissible to call what is heard from creation 'the speech of Allah'?
A) By way of literal reality.
B) By way of agreement (muwāfaqa) metaphorically.
C) By way of innovation.
D) By way of doubt.

Key Takeaway
The audible recitation of the Quran can be metaphorically called God's speech because it agrees with His eternal speech, just as a recited poem is attributed to its author.

Proof That God's Speech Is Unlike Created Speech
Imam Maturidi proves God's speech is unlike created speech using Quran and reason.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational and scriptural proof that God's speech is fundamentally unlike created speech, and why this negates temporality and accident-like attributes.

Core Idea
God's speech is utterly distinct from all created speech, just as His essence is distinct.

This passage from Imam Maturidi's Kitab al-Tawhid presents a multi-faceted argument that God's speech cannot be compared to human speech. Using Quranic verses and rational reasoning, Maturidi establishes that God's speech is free from the limitations and accidental attributes that characterize created speech. This lesson guides you through the key steps of this proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the source text
First, read the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully. Notice the flow from premise to evidence to conclusion.
The passage uses both Quranic citations and logical reasoning.
2
Identify the initial premise
The passage begins by stating that God's speech does not arise from incapacity or silence, unlike human speech. This sets up the contrast.
Human speech often results from need or prior silence, but God's speech is free from such limitations.
3
Analyze the Quranic evidence
Two Quranic verses are cited: 'There is nothing like Him' (42:11) and 'They created like His creation' (13:16). These negate any likeness in attribute and essence, and show that similarity in action would imply likeness, which is impossible for creation to produce.
The verse from 13:16 is a rhetorical question implying that false deities cannot create anything like God's creation.
4
Consider the examples of non-human speech
Maturidi mentions the speech of the ant, the hoopoe, and the glorification of mountains. These are not understood through human letters or language, demonstrating that God's speech transcends human comprehension.
This reinforces that God's speech is beyond human measurement or comparison.
5
Understand the conclusion
The passage concludes that God's speech is different from all created speech in every respect, and this difference negates temporality and accidents like separation, union, limit, increase, and decrease.
The negation of temporality implies that God's speech is eternal and uncreated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام فعن عجز لا يتكلم أو عن سكوت. ثم لا يخلو من أن يكون على تقدير كلام غيره فيكون فيه تشابه، ودل قوله: {وليس كمثله شيء} على نفي الشبه له في الصفة والذات؛ وأيد ذا قوله: {خلقوا كخلقه} الآية، دل أن شبه الفعل يوجب التشابه مع القول أن الخلق لو اجتمع لا يأتون بمثله، فانتفى الشبه، إذ فيه تماثل. فثبت له الخلافية لكلام الخلق جميعا على ما ثبت لذاته. مع ما لم يمتحن جميع كلام الخلق ليدرك منتهى معانيه. وقد ذكر كلام النمل والهدهد وتسبيح الجبال وغيرها مما لا يفهم شيء من ذلك بالحروف المعجمة ولا على المفهوم من كلام البشر. وإذ ثبت أن من الكلام ما لا يبلغ تقديره وسع الخلق ولا يبلغه فهم، فمن أحب تقدير كلام الرب بذلك فهو مغفل وكذلك فعله تعالى خارج عن وصف فعل الخلق. وفي ثبوت الخلافية من جميع الوجوه نفي الحدثية، لما بها يقع الوفاق؛ وبطل معنى الأعراض من التفرق والاجتماع، والحد والغاية والزيادة والنقصان، إذ ذلك وصف كلام الخلق. والله الموفق.
Speech is not from incapacity nor from silence. Then it is not free from being on the pattern of another's speech, in which case there would be likeness. And His saying 'And there is nothing like Him' (42:11) indicates the negation of likeness to Him in attribute and essence. And this is supported by His saying 'They created like His creation' (13:16) which indicates that similarity in action necessitates likeness, along with the statement that if all creation gathered they could not produce its like. So likeness is negated, for it would imply similarity. So it is established that His speech is different from all the speech of creation, just as it is established for His essence. And there has not been examined all the speech of creation to perceive the utmost of its meanings. And He has mentioned the speech of the ant, the hoopoe, and the glorification of the mountains, and other things that are not understood by articulated letters nor by the conventional understanding of human speech. And since it is established that there is speech whose estimation does not reach the capacity of creation nor does understanding reach it, then whoever wishes to measure the speech of the Lord by that is ignorant. Likewise, His action is outside the description of the action of creation. And in establishing the difference in all respects lies the negation of temporality, for by it agreement occurs. And the meaning of accidents — separation, union, limit, end, increase, and decrease — is invalidated, for that is the description of the speech of creation. And God grants success.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a rational and scriptural proof that God's speech is fundamentally unlike created speech. It begins by noting that God's speech does not arise from incapacity or silence, unlike human speech. It then uses a logical argument: if God's speech were like another's speech, it would involve likeness (tashabuh), but the Quranic verse 'There is nothing like Him' negates all likeness in attribute and essence. The verse 'They created like His creation' (13:16) further shows that similarity in action would imply likeness, yet creation cannot produce the like of God's speech, so likeness is negated. Thus, God's speech is utterly distinct (mukhalif) from created speech. The author supports this with examples from the Quran: the speech of the ant, the hoopoe, and the glorification of mountains — these are not understood through human letters or language, showing that God's speech is beyond human comprehension. Therefore, anyone who tries to measure God's speech by human standards is ignorant. The conclusion is that God's speech is free from the temporal attributes of accidents (a'rad) like separation, union, limit, increase, and decrease, which characterize created speech. This establishes that God's speech is uncreated and eternal.

Key Terms
خلاف
شبه
حدوث
عرض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Assuming that God's speech is like human speech in being composed of letters and sounds and subject to limitations.
Correction: The passage demonstrates that God's speech is not from incapacity or silence, is not patternable after another's speech, and includes examples like the ant's speech which is not understood through conventional language. Thus, God's speech is utterly different and free from temporal and accidental attributes.

Checkpoint
What does Imam Maturidi prove by citing the verse 'There is nothing like Him'?
A) That God's speech is created.
B) That God has no likeness in attribute and essence.
C) That God's speech is composed of letters.
D) That human speech is similar to God's speech.

Key Takeaway
God's speech is uncreated, eternal, and utterly unlike human speech, free from all temporal and accidental attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear the Quran recited, do you unconsciously treat it like human speech, or do you feel in your heart that it is the eternal, uncreated word of Allah? What would change in your reverence if you truly internalized that it is utterly unlike any other speech?
?
The passage says that even mountains glorify Allah in a way beyond human understanding. Have you ever considered that the whole creation is speaking to Allah in ways you cannot comprehend? How should that humiliate your pride in your own worship?
?
If God's speech is free from incapacity and silence, then every word of the Quran is from perfect power and knowledge. How does this challenge your moments of boredom or inattentiveness when reciting or listening to the Quran? What practical step can you take today to approach the Quran as speech that is 'not from incapacity nor from silence'?

God's Speech Is by Himself, Not by Another
Maturidi argues against speech being through another.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Maturidi's logical argument that God's speech is an essential attribute, not dependent on anything external.

Core Idea
God's speech is by His own essence, not through another, because that would imply need and temporality.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi presents a concise logical proof that God's attribute of speech cannot be acquired from something outside His essence. He uses a dichotomy to show that if speech came through another, it would indicate imperfection and temporality—impossible for Allah. The argument reinforces the Maturidi position that divine attributes are eternal and inherent.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the flow of the argument. Notice the use of 'ghayr' (other) and 'nafsihi' (Himself).
2
Identify the dichotomy
The passage presents two possibilities: either God's speech is through another or it is not through another.
3
Analyze the first possibility
If speech were through another, that other would remove defect, but that very fact indicates need (haja) and is a mark of temporality (hadath).
This is impossible for God.
4
Draw the conclusion
Since the first possibility is impossible, the second must be true: God's speech is not through another; He is speaking by His own essence, and He is powerful and knowing.
5
Reflect on the theological significance
This establishes that speech is an essential attribute of God, not dependent on any external cause, preserving divine perfection and eternity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم لا يخلو من أن يكون غيره فيزول عنه ما ذكرنا من الآفة بغيره ـ وذلك علم الحاجة وأمارة الحدث - أو ليس غيره فيكون بنفسه متكلما قادرا عالما. وبالله التوفيق.
Then it is not free from being other than Him, so what we mentioned of defect would cease by that other — and that is the sign of need and mark of temporality — or it is not other than Him, so He is by Himself speaking, powerful, knowing. And with God is success.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage presents a simple logical dichotomy to prove that God's speech is an essential attribute, not something acquired through another. The argument is: either God's speech is through something other than Himself (ghayr) or it is not. If it is through another, then that other would remove the defects (like need and temporality) that we have previously mentioned as belonging to created speech — but that would indicate need and temporality in God, which is impossible. Therefore, God's speech is not through another; rather, He is speaking by His own essence (bi nafsihi), and He is powerful and knowing. This reaffirms that God's speech is an eternal attribute of His essence.

Key Terms
غير
حادث
صفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God's speech is an accidental attribute that depends on something external (a created voice or letters).
Correction: The passage shows that if speech depended on another, it would imply need and temporality in God, which is impossible. Therefore, speech is an eternal essential attribute.

Checkpoint

A) It would be perfect.
B) It would indicate need and temporality.
C) It would be uncreated.
D) It would be identical to God.

Key Takeaway
God's speech is an eternal essential attribute, not dependent on any external cause, because dependence would imply imperfection and temporality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The passage states that if God's speech were through another, it would imply need and temporality. Have you ever, even unintentionally, attributed any form of need to God in your understanding of His attributes? Examine yourself and correct your belief right now.

Calling Heard Speech God's Speech: Metaphorical Attribution
Imam Maturidi explains that heard speech can be called God's speech metaphorically.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Maturidi considers it permissible to call the recited Qur'an God's speech metaphorically and the rational proof for this attribution.

Core Idea
Heard speech is attributed to God by agreement, not literally.

Imam Maturidi addresses a key question: in what sense can we call the audible recitation of the Qur'an 'God's speech'? He argues that it is permissible by way of agreement (muwafaqa), providing a proof based on the impossibility of a created accident or body being God Himself. The passage clarifies the relationship between the eternal speech of Allah and its created expression.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Maturidi uses a concise and structured argument style.
2
Understand the key terms
Focus on the term 'ala al-muwafaqa (by way of agreement) and the proof structure. Maturidi uses a logical disjunction (accident, body, neither) to show the impossibility of the heard speech being God Himself.
3
Examine the disjunction
Consider each possibility: if the heard speech is an accident, it cannot be in two places; if a body, likewise; if neither, it cannot be in a place, yet it is heard from a place. This establishes that the heard speech cannot be identical with God's eternal speech.
This is the core rational proof.
4
Reflect on the analogies
Maturidi gives two analogies: hearing another person's speech through a medium, and knowing God's power through creation. Both show that the medium is not the original. This reinforces the idea of metaphorical attribution.
These analogies help to clarify the concept.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز القول بما يسمع من الخلق كلام الله على الموافقة كما يقال في الرسائل والقصائد والأقاويل. دليله أن ذلك خلق من الخلق، ولا يحتمل أن يكون الله بذاته. مع ما لا يخلو من أن يكون المسموع عرضا - فمحال كونه في مكانين - وكذلك الجسم؛ أو لا هما، فمحال كونه في مكان؛ وعن المكان يسمع. فثبت أن وجه الإضافة إليه على ما ذكرنا. مع ما يجوز أن يسمعنا الله كلامه بما ليس بكلامه، كما أسمع كل منا آخر كلامه وإن لم يكن ذلك بعينه كلامه، وكما أعلمنا قدرته وعلمه وربوبيته بخلقه وإن لم يكن هو هو. وبالله التوفيق.
And it is permissible to say concerning what is heard from creation that it is the speech of God by way of agreement, just as it is said in letters and poems and sayings. Its proof is that that is a creation from creation, and it is not possible that it is God Himself. And with that, it is not free from being that the heard is an accident — so it is impossible for it to be in two places — and likewise a body; or neither of them, so it is impossible for it to be in a place; and from a place it is heard. So it is established that the mode of attribution to Him is as we mentioned. And with that, it is permissible for God to make us hear His speech by that which is not His speech, just as He makes each of us hear the speech of another even though that is not exactly his speech, and just as He makes us know His power, knowledge, and lordship through His creation even though it is not He Himself. And with God is success.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage addresses how to properly refer to the recitation of the Qur'an or the sounds heard from a human reader. It states that it is permissible to call that heard speech 'the speech of God' by way of agreement (ala al-muwafaqa), not literally. The proof is that the heard speech is a created thing (either an accident or a body), and it cannot be God Himself. If it is an accident, it cannot exist in two places simultaneously (e.g., in God and in the reciter); if it is a body, likewise; if it is neither, it cannot be in a place, yet it is heard from a place. Therefore, the attribution is metaphorical, not essential. The author gives analogies: God makes us hear another person's speech through a medium, and He makes us know His power through creation, even though the medium is not the same as the original. This clarifies that the Qur'an recited by humans is not identical with God's eternal speech but is a created representation.

Key Terms
موافقة
عرض
جسم
إضافة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that the recited Qur'an is literally God's uncreated speech in every respect.
Correction: Maturidi clarifies that the recited Qur'an is created and attributed to God metaphorically, not literally.

Checkpoint
What is the 'proof' given that the heard speech is not literally God's speech?
A) It is created and cannot be God Himself.
B) It is only heard by prophets.
C) It is written in a book.
D) It cannot be understood.

Key Takeaway
The recited Qur'an is created and attributed to God metaphorically, not literally.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you listen to the Qur'an being recited, do you ever pause to consider that the sound waves striking your ears are created things, yet they convey the very words of God? How does this distinction between the eternal speech and its created form change the way you approach recitation? Before your next prayer, take a moment to consciously acknowledge the miracle that God makes you hear His speech through created means, and let that awareness deepen your presence.
?
The lesson uses the analogy of a poem attributed to its author. Does this analogy ever make you feel that the recited Qur'an is somehow less sacred? Or does it instead protect God's transcendence by keeping His eternal attribute distinct from creation? Examine your own heart: Is your reverence for the Qur'an based more on its physical recitation or on its divine origin? Make a conscious effort to connect to the eternal meaning beyond the audible words during your next recitation.
?
Imam Maturidi argues that God makes us know His power, knowledge, and lordship through creation, but the creation is not itself those attributes. How often do you mistake the means for the end? When you read the Qur'an, do you stop at the beauty of the voice and the language, or do you let it lead you to the One who is speaking? Ask yourself: Am I content with the created form, or do I truly seek the uncreated Speech behind it?
